        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744"><meta property="og:title" content="Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS2 and 1T-WS2 by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/acsnano.8b07744.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="The phase-controlled synthesis of metallic and ambient-stable 2D MX2 (M is Mo or W; X is S) with 1T octahedral coordination will endow these materials with superior performance compared with their semiconducting 2H coordination counterparts. We report a clean and facile route to prepare 1T-MoS2 and 1T-WS2 through hydrothermal processing under high magnetic fields. We reveal that the as-synthesized 1T-MoS2 and 1T-WS2 are ambient-stable for more than 1 year. Electrochemical measurements show that 1T-MoS2 performs much better than 2H-MoS2 as the anode for sodium ion batteries. These results can provide a clean and facile method to prepare ambient-stable 1T-phase MX2."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/acsnano.8b07744.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6eec72a0d775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6eec72a0d775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '9471a43d-f5e9-4213-a276-c34d0c581d01'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90f6eec72a0d775c-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6eec72a0d775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'nano';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/nano/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/nano/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90f6eec72a0d775c-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "ancac3";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Highly Ambient-Stable 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; and 1T-WS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; by Hydrothermal Synthesis under High Magnetic Fields", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.8b07744", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_0006.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.8b07744&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">The phase-controlled synthesis of metallic and ambient-stable 2D MX<sub>2</sub> (M is Mo or W; X is S) with 1T octahedral coordination will endow these materials with superior performance compared with their semiconducting 2H coordination counterparts. We report a clean and facile route to prepare 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> through hydrothermal processing under high magnetic fields. We reveal that the as-synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> are ambient-stable for more than 1 year. Electrochemical measurements show that 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> performs much better than 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> as the anode for sodium ion batteries. These results can provide a clean and facile method to prepare ambient-stable 1T-phase MX<sub>2</sub>.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D1694%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DWei%2BDing%252C%2BLin%2BHu%252C%2BJianming%2BDai%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D2%26contentID%3Dacsnano.8b07744%26title%3DHighly%2BAmbient-Stable%2B1T-MoS2%2Band%2B1T-WS2%2Bby%2BHydrothermal%2BSynthesis%2Bunder%2BHigh%2BMagnetic%2BFields%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1936-0851%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dancac3%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D1702%26publicationDate%3DFebruary%2B2019" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright Â© 2019 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291880&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Crystal structure" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Crystal%20structure" class="article__tags__link">Crystal structure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290998&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Magnetic properties" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Magnetic%20properties" class="article__tags__link">Magnetic properties</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291758&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Scanning transmission electron microscopy" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Scanning%20transmission%20electron%20microscopy" class="article__tags__link">Scanning transmission electron microscopy</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292522&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Two dimensional materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Two%20dimensional%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Two dimensional materials</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Mos2&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_MoS2">MoS<sub>2</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Nanosheets&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_nanosheets">nanosheets</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Metallic+1T+Phase&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_metallic%201T%20phase">metallic 1T phase</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High+Magnetic+Fields&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high%20magnetic%20fields">high magnetic fields</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Hydrothermal&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_hydrothermal">hydrothermal</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="NLM_p first">Controllable phase synthesis of materials is desired because the crystal structure can obviously affect the properties. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 1 to 5">(1â5)</a> Transition-metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) MX<sub>2</sub> (M = Mo, W; X = S, Se, Te), as representative 2D materials, have been widely investigated recently because of their potential interesting applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 5 to 23">(5â23)</a> Importantly, the polymorphs of the MX<sub>2</sub> compounds such as MoS<sub>2</sub> and WS<sub>2</sub> usually show several types, including 1T and 2H phases, based on the different coordinating modes of M and X atoms. The 2H phase can be described as consisting of two SâMâS layers made up of edge-sharing MS<sub>6</sub> trigonal prisms, and the 1T phase is characterized in terms of one SâMâS layer built from edge-sharing MS<sub>6</sub> octahedra. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 24 to 28">(24â28)</a> Compared with its 2H phase counterpart with semiconducting characteristics, the 1T phase shows metallic behavior and has superior performances due to its high electrical conductivity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36" aria-label="reference 29 to 36">(29â36)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">From the thermodynamic viewpoint, the 1T polymorph is metastable, and the 2H phase is favored. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref37 ref38 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 7 and 37 to 39">(7,37â39)</a> Recently, several methods have been reported to synthesize 1T-MX<sub>2</sub>, such as alkali metal intercalation, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8 ref35 ref36 ref40 ref41 ref42 ref43 ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref35 ref36 ref40 ref41 ref42 ref43 ref44" aria-label="reference 8, 35, 36 and 40 to 44">(8,35,36,40â44)</a> mechanical exfoliation, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45 ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45 ref46" aria-label="reference 45 and 46">(45,46)</a> plasma hot electron transfer, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47" aria-label="reference 47">(47)</a> electron-beam irradiation, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> mechanical strains, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48 ref49 ref50 ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48 ref49 ref50 ref51" aria-label="reference 48 to 51">(48â51)</a> and hydrothermal reaction. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31 ref52'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref52" aria-label="reference 31 and 52">(31,52)</a> However, the as-synthesized 1T-MX<sub>2</sub> is easily converted into the 2H phase by contamination, the occurrence of intermediary phases, and oxidation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38 ref39 ref53'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38 ref39 ref53" aria-label="reference 38, 39 and 53">(38,39,53)</a> There has been no efficient route to synthesize clean and ambient-stable 1T-MX<sub>2</sub>. Magnetic fields as a type of important thermodynamic parameters in materials processing could transfer high energy on an atomic scale of substances, resulting in the expected atomic and molecular alignments. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54 ref55 ref56'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref54 ref55 ref56" aria-label="reference 54 to 56">(54â56)</a> Besides the manipulation of the morphology, the product phases can be tuned by applied magnetic fields in processing. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref57" aria-label="reference 57">(57)</a> Even metastable phases could be induced or stabilized by applied magnetic fields during synthesis processing, such as successful achievements of Î³-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and Î±-Co(OH)<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57 ref58 ref59'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref57 ref58 ref59" aria-label="reference 57 to 59">(57â59)</a> Because of the importance of magnetic fields in phase engineering, it is supposed that phase manipulation could be realized in MX<sub>2</sub> by magnetic fields.</div><div class="NLM_p last">We provide a facile strategy for the synthesis of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> by hydrothermal processing on a high-magnetic-field hydrothermal apparatus. Pure 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub>, showing high ambient-stability, were successfully synthesized by hydrothermal processing under high magnetic fields named as magneto-hydrothermal processing. Then, the synthesized products were characterized by transmission electron microscopy (TEM), X-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectroscopy, aberration-corrected scanning transmission electron microscopy (STEM), photoluminescence (PL), and X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). Furthermore, as the proof of suitability for applications, the ambient-stable 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets were employed as the anode for sodium ion batteries, showing excellent electrochemical performance as well as high stability after cycling with retention of the 1T crystal structure. We believe that magneto-hydrothermal processing will provide a clean route to synthesize ambient-stable 1T-MX<sub>2</sub>.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i3" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i3"> Sample Preparation and Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p">1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> were synthesized using a homemade magneto-hydrothermal apparatus, (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>), in which the magnetic field can reach as high as 10 T. The scanning electron microscope (SEM) images and the selected area electron diffraction (SAED) patterns (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S2 and S3</a>) reveal that the as-synthesized MoS<sub>2</sub> is composed of nanosheets with excellent crystalline quality. Meanwhile, the MoS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets show graphene-like morphologies with ripples and corrugations, and their thickness was reduced with increasing the applied magnetic fields during processing (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S3 and S4</a>). This tendency can be also observed from the atomic force microscopy (AFM) images (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>).</div><div class="NLM_p">The symmetry difference between the octahedral coordinated 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and the trigonal coordinated 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> crystal structures (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a) can be directly identified by high-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref60'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref60" aria-label="reference 5, 23 to 26 and 60">(5,23â26,60)</a> The HAADF-STEM images from the single-layer of the 9 T (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>bâe and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>) and 0 T magneto-hydrothermally synthesized MoS<sub>2</sub> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>fâh) directly show the differences in atomic arrangements. For the former one (MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T), the HAADF-STEM image (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b) shows a multilayered microstructure, as judged from the intensity profile (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>), and the S atoms are dispersed uniformly around the Mo atoms, leading to a strong contrast between S the and Mo sites (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c). In addition, the intensity ratio of S/Mo is â¼0.2, as shown in the inset image of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a> The diagonal atomic-scale edge structure (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d) and the crystalline ordering (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>e) confirm the 1T octahedral lattice. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref24 ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref24 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 12 and 24 to 26">(12,24â26)</a> In the latter one (MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T), honeycomb lattice intensity variations of the 2H phase are observed (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>), in which the two overlapping sulfur atoms can enhance the signal along the electron beam direction. As a result, the contrast of the S sites is close to that of the Mo sites, even though the atomic number (<i>Z</i>) of sulfur is lower. The intensity ratio of 2S/Mo is â¼0.7, as depicted in the inset image of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>f. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref22 ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref22 ref24" aria-label="reference 12, 22 and 24">(12,22,24)</a> The chevron-shaped atomic-scale edge structure (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>g) and the crystalline ordering (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>h) give evidence of the 2H trigonal lattice. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref24 ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref24 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 12 and 24 to 26">(12,24â26)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Crystal structure of MoS<sub>2</sub>. (a) Schematic of MoS<sub>2</sub> structures. (b) Top-view HAADF-STEM image of MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T. (c) Magnified top-view HAADF-STEM image from the area inside the white rectangle in panel b, indicating the 1T phase lattice arrangement. (The insert image gives the intensity profiles to show the atomic ratio between S and Mo from the area labeled with the yellow rectangle.) (d) Side-view annular bright-field (ABF) image of MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T. (e) Magnified side-view ABF image from the area inside the red rectangle in panel d; the side-view structure of 1T MoS<sub>2</sub> is also shown. (f) Magnified top-view HAADF-STEM image of MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T nanosheets indicating coordination around S and Mo atoms. (The insert images are the original top-view HAADF-STEM image of MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and the intensity profiles from the area labeled with the yellow rectangle.) (g) Side-view ABF image of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T nanosheets. (h) Magnified side-view ABF image from the area inside the blue rectangle of panel g; the side-view structures of 2H MoS<sub>2</sub> are also shown. (i) XRD and (j) Raman spectra of MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T and MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T. The blue dots indicate Mo atoms, and the yellow dots indicate S atoms in panels c, e, f, and h.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.8b07744&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">The crystal structures of the as-produced MoS<sub>2</sub> samples were investigated through XRD (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>i). The MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T shows a strong 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (002) peak at 2Î¸ = 14.38Â°, which is attributed to the interplanar spacing of 6.15 Ã, and it is consistent with the STEM data (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>g). Interestingly, for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T, the (002) and (004) diffraction peaks with interplanar distance of 9.4 and 4.7 Ã are observed, respectively, agreeing with the crystal structure of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref61 ref62'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref61 ref62" aria-label="reference 23, 61 and 62">(23,61,62)</a> As seen from the Raman spectra (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>j), for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T nanosheets, two typical Raman peaks at wavelength of â¼378 and 404 cm<sup>â1</sup> are evident from the E<sub class="stack">2g</sub><sup class="stack">1</sup> and A<sub>1g</sub> modes, respectively, confirming the 2H crystal structure. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> Interestingly, additional peaks centered at 146 (J<sub>1</sub>), 234 (J<sub>2</sub>), and 335 (J<sub>3</sub>) cm<sup>â1</sup> can be clearly observed, which are believed to be from 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>, indicating the 1T crystal structure of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> Because of the semiconductor-like characterization of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and the metallic behavior of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>, a PL peak is observed for the former one, whereas no such PL peak appears for the latter one. The PL spectra (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>) show an obvious PL peak for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T, but no such PL peak is seen for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T, further confirming the 1T crystal structure of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref63'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref63" aria-label="reference 41 and 63">(41,63)</a> From the aforementioned results, it is interesting to observe that 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> can be successfully synthesized by magneto-hydrothermal processing. Additionally, 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> can also be synthesized by magneto-hydrothermal processing (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S10âS14</a>), suggesting the validity of magneto-hydrothermal processing for the preparation of 1T-MX<sub>2</sub>.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4"> Phase Engineering and Stability</h3><div class="NLM_p">As has been seen, 1T-MX<sub>2</sub> can be synthesized through magneto-hydrothermal processing, and it is interesting to investigate the function of the magnetic field strength in processing. HAADF-STEM observations from the single-layer of the MoS<sub>2</sub> prepared under different magnetic fields in magneto-hydrothermal processing were therefore carried out (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15</a>). The as-synthesized MoS<sub>2</sub> under zero magnetic field processing is also composed of a small fraction of 1T phase (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a,b), which can be attributed to some content of S vacancies in the as-synthesized nanosheets (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S16 and Table S1</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref64" aria-label="reference 64">(64)</a> Interestingly, the 1T phase is obviously expanded by increasing the applied magnetic fields in magneto-hydrothermal processing, such as for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-8T (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c,d), and pure 1T phase is obtained under 9T (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c). The percentage of 1T phase in the as-synthesized 1T-MX<sub>2</sub> can be calculated from the XPS spectra because the binding energy of the 1T phase is lower than that of the 2H counterpart by â¼0.8 eV. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref41 ref65'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref41 ref65" aria-label="reference 23, 41 and 65">(23,41,65)</a> By deconvoluting the XPS peaks (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a), the percentage of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> synthesized under 0, 5, 8, and 9 T is, respectively, estimated to be 24.7, 48.9, 76.4, and 100% (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b). Similarly, the percentage of 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> synthesized under 0 and 8 T is estimated to be â¼60 and 100%, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14</a>).</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) HAADF-STEM image of MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T. (b) Magnified top-view HAADF-STEM image from the area inside the blue rectangle in panel a, from which a small fraction of 1T phase is observed and the intensity profiles from the selected areas confirm the 2H and 1T phases. (c) HAADF-STEM images of MoS<sub>2</sub>-8T. (d) Magnified top-view HAADF-STEM image from the area inside the yellow rectangle in panel c, from which a high fraction of 1T phase is observed and the intensity profiles from the selected areas confirm the 2H and 1T phases. The green area indicates the 1T phase, and the red area indicates the 2H phase.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.8b07744&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) XPS results of the as-synthesized MoS<sub>2</sub> processed under different magnetic fields in magneto-hydrothermal processing. (b) Phase percentage of MoS<sub>2</sub> from deconvolution of XPS spectra.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.8b07744&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">The stability of 1T-MX<sub>2</sub> is very important for applications. In general, 1T MX<sub>2</sub> is metastable, and it is usually observed that 1T phase is gradually converted into 2H phase. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 38 and 39">(38,39)</a> The XRD (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S17</a>), HAADF-STEM (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S18</a>), and XPS (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S19</a>) results for the magneto-hydrothermally synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> after aging for 1 year reveal no obvious changes. It is surprising to observe that the 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> obtained by magneto-hydrothermal processing show high ambient stability, confirming the advantages of magneto-hydrothermal processing for the preparation of 1T-MX<sub>2</sub>. In general, the formation energy of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> is â¼0.5 eV lower than that of the stoichiometric 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> phase, leading to the thermodynamically preferred 2H phase. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> Interestingly, with the appearance of S vacancies, the difference in formation energy between 2H and 1T phase decreases due to the extra electrons induced by S vacancies, so that it can be close to zero but still above zero when the vacancy concentration reaches 8 at % in MoS<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref64" aria-label="reference 64">(64)</a> It is worth noting that pure 1T-MX<sub>2</sub> cannot be directly obtained through simple S-vacancy manipulation in our processing because large amounts of S vacancies will lead to the collapse of the crystal structure. Here the ratios of Mo/S and W/S are determined to be 1:1.89 and 1:1.75 for the synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub>, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>). The 4d electrons in the trigonal prismatic crystal field of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> are split into d<sub><i>x</i></sub><sup>2</sup><sub>ây</sub><sup>2</sup>/d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>, d<sub><i>yz</i></sub>/d<sub><i>xz</i></sub>, and d<sub><i>z</i></sub><sup>2</sup> orbitals, showing no unpaired spins and diamagnetism. On the contrary, the 4d electrons in the octahedral prismatic crystal field of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> are split into d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>, d<sub><i>yz</i></sub>, and d<sub><i>xz</i></sub> degenerate orbitals and d<sub><i>z</i></sub><sup>2</sup> and d<sub><i>x</i></sub><sup>2</sup><sub>ây</sub><sup>2</sup> degenerate orbitals, leading to a net magnetic moment on Mo atoms. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref66'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref66" aria-label="reference 66">(66)</a> In magneto-hydrothermal processing, with the introduction of magnetic fields, an extra free energy, called magnetic free energy, <span class="NLM_inline-formula"><i class="MathJaxEquation"></i><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer inline-formula-styles" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i5"></span>, will be induced, in which <i>Î¼</i><sub>0</sub> is the permeability of vacuum, Ï is the volumetric magnetic susceptibility, <i>V</i> is the volume, and <i>H</i> is the magnetic field strength. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56 ref58'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref56 ref58" aria-label="reference 56 and 58">(56,58)</a> Because the 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> shows a higher Ï than that of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S20</a>), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref66'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref66" aria-label="reference 66">(66)</a> the ground-state energy of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> will be lowered in magneto-hydrothermal processing compared with the 2H phase. Additionally, the <i>E</i><sub>M</sub> will be decreased with <i>B</i><sup>2</sup>, resulting in the gradual enhancement of the concentration of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> with increasing magnetic field in magneto-hydrothermal processing; finally, nearly pure 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> can be obtained, as confirmed by the PL result without PL emission peaks due to the metallic characteristic (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>). As for the long-time stability of the synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>, the magnetostatic energy should be considered. The magnetostatic energy Î¼ is described as <span class="NLM_inline-formula"><i class="MathJaxEquation"></i><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer inline-formula-styles" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i6"></span>, where Î¼<sub>0</sub> is the vacuum magnetic permeability, <i>N</i> is the demagnetization factor, and <i>M</i> is the magnetic moment. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref67'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref67" aria-label="reference 67">(67)</a> The magnetic moment is enhanced with increasing magnetic field in magneto-hydrothermal processing, resulting in the decreased magnetostatic energy (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S20</a>), which will lead to the long-time stability for the synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> samples.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p">As a proof of suitability for electrochemical applications, the as-synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> were used to construct half cells using sodium metals as the counter electrodes, respectively. The capacity versus voltage (<i>CâV</i>) measurements of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T were carried out in the potential window of 0.3â3 V at a current density of 1 A g<sup>â1</sup>. The MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T electrode delivered the initial discharge and charge capacities with 401 and 314 mA h g<sup>â1</sup>, respectively. The shapes of the <i>CâV</i> profiles, however, obviously changed during the following cycling (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a), suggesting lower reversibility and structural stability during the processes of sodiation and desodiation. As for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrode, the first discharge and charge capacities are 385 and 304 mA h g<sup>â1</sup>, respectively.(<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b). Interestingly, the shapes of the charge/discharge profiles are similar to each other after the first cycle, indicating highly reversible sodium storage. Moreover, the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T exhibits more excellent rate performance (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c), showing reversible discharge capacity with 293 mA h g<sup>â1</sup> at a current density of 1 A g<sup>â1</sup>. Even when cycled at 8 A g<sup>â1</sup>, the specific capacity reached 224 mA h g<sup>â1</sup>. In addition, to investigate the high-rate cycling performance, the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T anodes were subjected to prolonged cycling at 1 A g<sup>â1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d). The MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T reaches the initial discharge capacity with 385 mA h g<sup>â1</sup> and retains a high discharge capacity with 310 mA h g<sup>â1</sup> after 280 cycles, which is higher than that of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T with the discharge capacity of 182 mA h g<sup>â1</sup> after 280 cycles.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Electrochemical measurements: Discharge/charge curves of (a) MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and (b) MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrode. (c) Rate performance for MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T. (d) Cycling performance for MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T at 1 A g<sup>â1</sup>. (e,f) AC impedance plots for fresh and after five cycles at 1 A g<sup>â1</sup> from 0.1 Hz to 100 kHz, respectively. (g) Electronic density of states (DOS) for MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T, in which the Fermi level is set to zero (dashed line). (h) Chemical diffusion coefficient of sodium ions as a function of voltage calculated by GITT.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.8b07744&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To reveal the electrochemical performance, electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) measurements were carried out using the cells at the stable state. The plots consist of a straight line at low frequency relative to the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and a high-frequency semicircle depending on the charge-transfer resistance at the electrode and electrolyte interface (<i>R</i><sub>c</sub><sub>t</sub>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref68" aria-label="reference 68">(68)</a> From the EIS plots of the cells before (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>e) and after five cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>f), one can see that the semicircles of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrode are much smaller than those of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T electrode, indicating lower charge-transfer resistance for the former one for both the fresh and the cycled conditions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref69'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref69" aria-label="reference 69">(69)</a> For further illustration, the electronic densities of states (DOS) of MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T and MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T were carried out using first-principles density functional theory (DFT) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>g). It is seen that the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T is a semiconductor with a band gap of â¼1 eV, whereas the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T is metallic. It is well known that the electronic conductivity is the most important factor influencing the rate capability of the anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). The small resistance will lead to a small amount of heat during the charging and discharging process, which is beneficial for the long life and safety of the batteries. To further investigate the kinetics, galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements within the voltage window of 0.3â3 V were performed (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S21</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref70'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref70" aria-label="reference 70">(70)</a> Accordingly, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient, <i>D</i>, can be calculated as <span class="NLM_inline-formula"><i class="MathJaxEquation"></i><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer inline-formula-styles" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_m003.gif" alt="" id="_i8"></span>, where Ï is the titration time, <i>L</i> is the thickness of the electrode, Î<i>E</i><sub>s</sub> is the difference between two consecutive stabilized open-circuit voltages, and Î<i>E<sub>Ï</sub></i> is the total change in the cell voltage during a constant current pulse excluding the IR drop (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S22</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref70'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref70" aria-label="reference 70">(70)</a> It is observed that the diffusion coefficient of MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T is significantly higher than that of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>h). The enhanced <i>D</i> of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrode is ascribed to a lower barrier for the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction because of the bigger <i>d</i> spacing of the 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref68" aria-label="reference 68">(68)</a> resulting in the improved electrochemical performance.</div><div class="NLM_p">Furthermore, to give a clear picture of the 1T structural stability after cycling, HAADF-STEM observations were carried out on the discharged MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrode after the 125th cycle at 1 A g<sup>â1</sup>. The elemental mapping results revealed that Mo and S coexist, and they are distributed uniformly after 125 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>aâd). The multilayered structure is effectively maintained (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e), and the <i>d</i> spacing between the layers is also maintained as 0.942 nm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>f). The magnified top-view (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>g) and side-view HAADF-STEM (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>h) images clearly show that the 1T octahedral lattice arrangements are conserved, further confirming the high structural stability of the 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>. Additionally, the measurements of the electrochemical properties for the synthesized MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrodes aged for 1 year have been carried out, and the results show that the electrochemical properties are slightly degraded, confirming the long-time stability of the magneto-hydrothermal synthesized MoS<sub>2</sub> samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S23</a>). As for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T electrode, the nanosheets are broken into small fragments after 125 cycles at 1 A g<sup>â1</sup>, which is similar to previous reports due to the small interlayer spacing of the 2H phase (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S24</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68 ref71'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref68 ref71" aria-label="reference 68 and 71">(68,71)</a></div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/medium/nn-2018-07744n_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. STEM observations of the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T electrode after 125 cycles at 1 A g<sup>â1</sup>: (a) STEM image. (bâd) Energy-dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) elemental mappings. (e) Typical top-view HAADF-STEM image from the area inside the green rectangle of panel a. (f) Typical side-view annular bright-field (ABF) image from the area inside the yellow rectangle of panel a. (g) Magnified top-view HAADF-STEM image for a single layer from the area inside the blue circles of panel e, showing coordination around the Mo and S atoms. (h) Magnified side-view ABF image indicated by the area in the red rectangle in panel f, with the coordination of atoms around Mo and S shown at the top. (Yellow and blue dots, respectively, indicate the S and Mo atoms in panels g and h.)</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/asset/images/large/nn-2018-07744n_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.8b07744&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">Magneto-hydrothermal processing as a facile and clean route to synthesize 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> was developed. The 1T octahedral coordination structure was confirmed by XRD, XPS, PL, Raman spectroscopy, and STEM. The as-synthesized 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-WS<sub>2</sub> samples are ambient-stable, showing long-time stability for more than 1 year. A superior electrochemical performance of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> as the anode in sodium ion batteries was observed with a specific capacity of 224 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> at a high current density of 8 A g<sup>â1</sup>. This excellent performance originates from its enhanced kinetics and stable 1T octahedral coordination, as confirmed by GITT and STEM measurements. Our findings will open up a clean and facile way to synthesize ambient-stable 2D 1T-MX<sub>2</sub> materials for applications in electrochemical devices.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i10">Experimental Methods</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec4_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i11" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i11"> Preparation of MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets</h3><div class="NLM_p last">(NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>6</sub>Mo<sub>7</sub>O<sub>24</sub>Â·4H<sub>2</sub>O (CAS number 12027-67-7) and thiourea (CAS number 62-56-6) were purchased from Alfa Aesar. All chemicals were used without any further purification. 1.4209 g thiourea and 0.7242 g (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>6</sub>Mo<sub>7</sub>O<sub>24</sub>Â·4H<sub>2</sub>O were dissolved in deionized water (21.8 mL) and stirred vigorously for 30 min to get a homogeneous solution. After the mixture was transferred to a Teflon-lined stainless-steel autoclave (28 mL capacity), a magnetic field was applied. Then, it was heated to 210 Â°C in 40 min and kept for 18 h under different magnetic fields. After synthesis, when the temperature was decreased to 80 Â°C, the magnetic field was then removed and the reaction system was naturally cooled to room temperature. The resulting product was filtered, washed several times by deionized water and ethanol, and finally dried at 70 Â°C in a vacuum oven.</div></div><div id="sec4_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i12" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i12"> Preparation of WS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets</h3><div class="NLM_p last">WCl<sub>6</sub> (CAS number 13283-01-7) and thioacetamide (TAA, CAS number 62-55-5) were purchased from Sigma-Aldrich. All chemicals were used without any further purification. 0.61 g tungsten chloride and 1.17 g TAA were dissolved in deionized water (20.5 mL) and stirred vigorously for 30 min. After the mixture was transferred to a Teflon-lined stainless-steel autoclave (26 mL capacity), a magnetic field was applied. Then, it was heated to 210 Â°C in 40 min and kept for 24 h under different magnetic fields. When the temperature was decreased to 80 Â°C, the magnetic field was removed, and the reaction system was naturally cooled to room temperature. The product was filtered, washed several times by deionized water and absolute ethanol, and finally dried at 70 Â°C in a vacuum oven.</div></div><div id="sec4_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i13" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i13"> Electrochemical Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The electrochemical tests were carried out with CR2032 cells assembled in a glovebox filled with argon. The MoS<sub>2</sub> electrodes were produced by mixing active material (80 wt %), Super P (10 wt %), and carboxymethyl cellulose (CMC) (10 wt %) in deionized water. The resultant slurry was coated on Cu foil and dried at 80 Â°C for overnight in vacuum, which was followed by pressing under 20 MPa in a table compression machine. Electrochemical measurements were conducted with coin half cells. Glass fiber was used as the separator, and sodium foil served as the counter electrode. The electrolyte was a solution of 1 M sodium trifluoromethane-sulfonate in diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (DEGDME), which was free from H<sub>2</sub>O. A Landt CT2001 cell testing system was used for galvanostatic chargeâdischarge tests between 0.3 and 3 V. A VMP-3 electrochemical workstation was used for in situ EIS measurement.</div></div><div id="sec4_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i14" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i14"> Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Field-emission scanning electron microscope (FE-SEM) images were collected on a JEOL JSM-6700F SEM. High-resolution transmission electron microscope (HRTEM) images were collected on a JEOL-2011 TEM operated at an acceleration voltage of 200 kV. HAADF-STEM images were collected on a JEOL JEM-ARM200F at an acceleration voltage of 80 kV. Specimens for STEM characterization were prepared by dropping an ethanol suspension of the as-prepared MoS<sub>2</sub>/WS<sub>2</sub> onto amorphous carbon-coated copper grids. For top-view images, the edge regions of horizontally placed nanosheets were searched for single-layer regions. Nanosheets placed vertically were searched to get the side-view images (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.8b07744/suppl_file/nn8b07744_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S25</a>). The XPS was obtained on an ESCALAB MK II device with Mg KÎ± as the excitation source. Raman spectroscopy was carried out by a LabRAM HR800 UV NIR spectrometer with 532 nm laser excitation. XRD was carried out on a Philips XâPert Pro Super diffractometer with Cu KÎ± radiation (Î» = 1.54178 Ã). Magnetization studies were performed using a superconducting quantum interference device (SQUID) magnetometer. The PL spectra were obtained with a Nd:YAG laser (Î» = 532 nm).</div></div><div id="sec4_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i15" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i15"> Density Functional Theory Calculations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The DFT calculations were carried out by Quantum ESPRESSO <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref72'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref72" aria-label="reference 72">(72)</a> with ultrasoft pseudopotentials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref73'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref73" aria-label="reference 73">(73)</a> The exchange and correlation effects were processed within the generalized gradient approximation (GGA). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref74'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref74" aria-label="reference 74">(74)</a> Deficient MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T was simulated using a 2 Ã 2 Ã 4 supercell with two S vacancies. In the irreducible Brillouin zone, we used the plane-wave cutoff energy of 60 Ry and 16 Ã 16 Ã 8 <i>k</i>-point mesh in the irreducible Brillouin zone for stoichiometric MoS<sub>2</sub>-0T, along with a 16 Ã 16 Ã 1 <i>k</i>-point mesh for the MoS<sub>2</sub>-9T (1T-MoS<sub>1.875</sub>) supercell. The van der Waals interaction correction DFT-D<sub>2</sub> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref75 ref76'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref75 ref76" aria-label="reference 75 and 76">(75,76)</a> was used to avoid overestimation of the interlayer distance.</div></div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div
